<p>The <b>Three Gorges Dam</b> is a <a href="/wiki/Hydroelectricity" title="Hydroelectricity">hydroelectric</a> dam that spans the <a href="/wiki/Yangtze_River" class="mw-redirect" title="Yangtze River">Yangtze River</a> by the town of <a href="/wiki/Sandouping" title="Sandouping">Sandouping</a>, located in <a href="/wiki/Yiling_District" title="Yiling District">Yiling District</a>, <a href="/wiki/Yichang" title="Yichang">Yichang</a>, <a href="/wiki/Hubei" title="Hubei">Hubei</a> province, <a href="/wiki/China" title="China">China</a>. The Three Gorges Dam is the <a href="/wiki/List_of_largest_power_stations_in_the_world" class="mw-redirect" title="List of largest power stations in the world">world's largest power station</a> in terms of <a href="/wiki/Installed_capacity" class="mw-redirect" title="Installed capacity">installed capacity</a> (22,500&#160;<a href="/wiki/Megawatt" class="mw-redirect" title="Megawatt">MW</a>). In 2014 the dam generated 98.8 <a href="/wiki/Kilowatt_hour#Multiples" title="Kilowatt hour">terawatt-hours</a> (TWh) of electricity, setting a new world record by 0.17 TWh previously held by the <a href="/wiki/Itaip%C3%BA_Dam" class="mw-redirect" title="Itaipú Dam">Itaipú Dam</a> on the <a href="/wiki/Brazil" title="Brazil">Brazil</a>/<a href="/wiki/Paraguay" title="Paraguay">Paraguay</a> border in 2013 of 98.63.<sup id="cite_ref-4" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-4">[4]</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-5" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-5">[5]</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-6" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-6">[6]</a></sup> In 2015, the Itaipu power plant resumed the lead in annual worldwide production, producing 89.5 TWh, while production of Three Gorges was 87 TWh.<sup id="cite_ref-7" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-7">[7]</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-8" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-8">[8]</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-9" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-9">[9]</a></sup></p>
<p>Except for the locks, the dam project was completed and fully functional as of July 4, 2012,<sup id="cite_ref-autogenerated5_10-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-autogenerated5-10">[10]</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-11" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-11">[11]</a></sup> when the last of the main <a href="/wiki/Water_turbine" title="Water turbine">water turbines</a> in the underground plant began production. The ship lift was complete in December 2015.<sup id="cite_ref-shipcom_12-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-shipcom-12">[12]</a></sup> Each main water turbine has a capacity of 700&#160;MW.<sup id="cite_ref-iet2009_13-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-iet2009-13">[13]</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-ctgpc1_14-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-ctgpc1-14">[14]</a></sup> The dam body was completed in 2006. Coupling the dam's 32 main turbines with two smaller generators (50&#160;MW each) to power the plant itself, the total electric generating capacity of the dam is 22,500&#160;MW.<sup id="cite_ref-iet2009_13-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-iet2009-13">[13]</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-Xinhua20081007_15-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Xinhua20081007-15">[15]</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-inventspot_16-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-inventspot-16">[16]</a></sup></p>
<p>As well as producing electricity, the dam is intended to increase the Yangtze River's shipping capacity and reduce the potential for floods downstream by providing flood storage space. China regards the project as monumental as well as a success socially and economically,<sup id="cite_ref-17" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-17">[17]</a></sup> with the design of state-of-the-art large turbines,<sup id="cite_ref-18" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-18">[18]</a></sup> and a move toward limiting <a href="/wiki/Greenhouse_gas" title="Greenhouse gas">greenhouse gas</a> emissions.<sup id="cite_ref-19" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-19">[19]</a></sup> However, the dam flooded <a href="/wiki/Archaeological" class="mw-redirect" title="Archaeological">archaeological</a> and cultural sites and displaced some 1.3&#160;million people, and is causing significant <a href="/wiki/Ecological" class="mw-redirect" title="Ecological">ecological</a> changes, including an increased risk of <a href="/wiki/Landslide" title="Landslide">landslides</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-20" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-20">[20]</a></sup> The dam has been controversial both domestically and abroad.<sup id="cite_ref-controversy_21-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-controversy-21">[21]</a></sup></p>
<table class="infobox" style="width: 22em">

<h2><span class="mw-headline" id="History">History</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Three_Gorges_Dam&amp;action=edit&amp;section=1" title="Edit section: History">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h2>
<div class="thumb tright">
<div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a href="/wiki/File:Wuhan-Flood-Memorial-0220.jpg" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/5/5b/Wuhan-Flood-Memorial-0220.jpg/220px-Wuhan-Flood-Memorial-0220.jpg" width="220" height="293" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/5/5b/Wuhan-Flood-Memorial-0220.jpg/330px-Wuhan-Flood-Memorial-0220.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/5/5b/Wuhan-Flood-Memorial-0220.jpg/440px-Wuhan-Flood-Memorial-0220.jpg 2x" data-file-width="1536" data-file-height="2048" /></a>
<div class="thumbcaption">
<div class="magnify"><a href="/wiki/File:Wuhan-Flood-Memorial-0220.jpg" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a></div>
In his poem "Swimming" (1956), engraved on the <a href="/wiki/1954_Yangtze_River_Floods" class="mw-redirect" title="1954 Yangtze River Floods">1954 Flood</a> Memorial in <a href="/wiki/Wuhan" title="Wuhan">Wuhan</a>, Mao Zedong envisions "walls of stone" to be erected upstream.<sup id="cite_ref-22" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-22">[22]</a></sup></div>
</div>
</div>
<p>A large dam across the Yangtze River was originally envisioned by <a href="/wiki/Sun_Yat-sen" title="Sun Yat-sen">Sun Yat-sen</a> in <i>The International Development of China</i>, in 1919.<sup id="cite_ref-23" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-23">[23]</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-autogenerated2006_24-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-autogenerated2006-24">[24]</a></sup> He stated that a dam capable of generating 30&#160;million horsepower (22&#160;GW) was possible downstream of the <a href="/wiki/Three_Gorges" title="Three Gorges">Three Gorges</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-autogenerated2006_24-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-autogenerated2006-24">[24]</a></sup> In 1932, the Nationalist government, led by <a href="/wiki/Chiang_Kai-shek" title="Chiang Kai-shek">Chiang Kai-shek</a>, began preliminary work on plans in the Three Gorges. In 1939, <a href="/wiki/Second_Sino-Japanese_War" title="Second Sino-Japanese War">Japanese military forces</a> occupied <a href="/wiki/Yichang" title="Yichang">Yichang</a> and surveyed the area. A design, the Otani plan, was completed for the dam in anticipation of a Japanese victory over <a href="/wiki/China" title="China">China</a>.</p>
<p>In 1944, the United States <a href="/wiki/Bureau_of_Reclamation" class="mw-redirect" title="Bureau of Reclamation">Bureau of Reclamation</a> chief design engineer, <a href="/wiki/John_L._Savage" title="John L. Savage">John L. Savage</a>, surveyed the area and drew up a dam proposal for the 'Yangtze River Project'.<sup id="cite_ref-nasbio_25-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-nasbio-25">[25]</a></sup> Some 54 Chinese engineers went to the U.S. for training. The original plans called for the dam to employ a unique method for moving ships; the ships would move into locks located at the lower and upper ends of the dam and then cranes with cables would move the ships from one lock to the next. In the case of smaller water craft, groups of craft would be lifted together for efficiency. It is not known whether this solution was considered for its water-saving performance or because the engineers thought the difference in height between the river above and below the dam too great for alternative methods.<sup id="cite_ref-26" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-26">[26]</a></sup> Some exploration, survey, economic study, and design work was done, but the government, in the midst of the <a href="/wiki/Chinese_Civil_War" title="Chinese Civil War">Chinese Civil War</a>, halted work in 1947.</p>
<p>After the 1949 Communist takeover, <a href="/wiki/Mao_Zedong" title="Mao Zedong">Mao Zedong</a> supported the project, but began the <a href="/wiki/Gezhouba_Dam" title="Gezhouba Dam">Gezhouba Dam</a> project nearby first, and economic problems including the <a href="/wiki/Great_Leap_Forward" title="Great Leap Forward">Great Leap Forward</a> and the <a href="/wiki/Cultural_Revolution" title="Cultural Revolution">Cultural Revolution</a> slowed progress. After the <a href="/wiki/1954_Yangtze_River_Floods" class="mw-redirect" title="1954 Yangtze River Floods">1954 Yangtze River Floods</a>, in 1956, Mao Zedong authored "Swimming", a poem about his fascination with a dam on the Yangtze River. In 1958, after the <a href="/wiki/Hundred_Flowers_Campaign" title="Hundred Flowers Campaign">Hundred Flowers Campaign</a>, some engineers who spoke out against the project were imprisoned.<sup id="cite_ref-WPhist_27-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-WPhist-27">[27]</a></sup></p>
<p>During the 1980s, the idea of a dam reemerged. The <a href="/wiki/National_People%27s_Congress" title="National People's Congress">National People's Congress</a> approved the dam in 1992: out of 2,633 delegates, 1,767 voted in favour, 177 voted against, 664 abstained, and 25 members did not vote.<sup id="cite_ref-28" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-28">[28]</a></sup> Construction started on December 14, 1994.<sup id="cite_ref-allin_29-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-allin-29">[29]</a></sup> The dam was expected to be fully operational in 2009, but additional projects, such as the underground <a href="/wiki/Power_plant" class="mw-redirect" title="Power plant">power plant</a> with six additional generators, delayed full operation until May 2012.<sup class="noprint Inline-Template" style="white-space:nowrap;">[<i><a href="/wiki/Wikipedia:Verifiability" title="Wikipedia:Verifiability"><span title="The material near this tag needs to be fact-checked with the cited source(s). (August 2015)">verification needed</span></a></i>]</sup><sup id="cite_ref-inventspot_16-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-inventspot-16">[16]</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-WPhist_27-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-WPhist-27">[27]</a></sup> The ship lift was completed in 2015.<sup id="cite_ref-shipcom_12-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-shipcom-12">[12]</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-CnHubei20071110_30-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-CnHubei20071110-30">[30]</a></sup> The dam had raised the water level in the reservoir to 172.5&#160;m (566&#160;ft) above sea level by the end of 2008 and the designed maximum level of 175&#160;m (574&#160;ft) by October 2010.<sup id="cite_ref-Xin2010_31-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Xin2010-31">[31]</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-32" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-32">[32]</a></sup></p>
<div class="thumb tnone" style="width:; max-width:608px;">
<div class="thumbinner" style="">
<div class="overflowbugx" style="overflow:auto;"><a href="/wiki/File:Threegorges.png" class="image" title="Map of the location of the Three Gorges Dam and the most important cities along the Yangtze River"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/4/4c/Threegorges.png/600px-Threegorges.png" width="600" height="226" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/4/4c/Threegorges.png 1.5x" data-file-width="690" data-file-height="260" /></a></div>
<div class="thumbcaption">
<div class="magnify"><a href="/wiki/File:Threegorges.png" title="File:Threegorges.png"></a></div>
Map of the location of the Three Gorges Dam and the most important cities along the Yangtze River</div>
</div>
</div>
<h2><span class="mw-headline" id="Composition_and_dimensions">Composition and dimensions</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Three_Gorges_Dam&amp;action=edit&amp;section=2" title="Edit section: Composition and dimensions">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h2>
<div class="thumb tmulti tright">
<div class="thumbinner" style="width:224px;max-width:224px">
<div class="tsingle" style="margin:1px;width:222px;max-width:222px">
<div class="thumbimage"><a href="/wiki/File:TGDModelSpillwayView.jpg" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/4/4a/TGDModelSpillwayView.jpg/220px-TGDModelSpillwayView.jpg" width="220" height="101" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/4/4a/TGDModelSpillwayView.jpg/330px-TGDModelSpillwayView.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/4/4a/TGDModelSpillwayView.jpg/440px-TGDModelSpillwayView.jpg 2x" data-file-width="512" data-file-height="234" /></a></div>
<div class="thumbcaption" style="clear:left">Model of the Three Gorges Dam looking upstream, showing the dam body (middle left), the spillway (middle of the dam body) and the ship lift (to the right).</div>
</div>
<div class="tsingle" style="margin:1px;width:222px;max-width:222px">
<div class="thumbimage"><a href="/wiki/File:TGDModelShipLocks.jpg" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/8/86/TGDModelShipLocks.jpg/220px-TGDModelShipLocks.jpg" width="220" height="122" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/8/86/TGDModelShipLocks.jpg/330px-TGDModelShipLocks.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/8/86/TGDModelShipLocks.jpg/440px-TGDModelShipLocks.jpg 2x" data-file-width="512" data-file-height="285" /></a></div>
<div class="thumbcaption" style="clear:left">Model of the Three Gorges Dam showing the ship lift and the ship lock. The ship lift is to the right of the dam body with its own designated waterway. The ship locks are to the right (northeast) of the ship lift.</div>
</div>
<div class="tsingle" style="margin:1px;width:222px;max-width:222px">
<div class="thumbimage"><a href="/wiki/File:TGDModelAuxSouthDam.jpg" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/6/67/TGDModelAuxSouthDam.jpg/220px-TGDModelAuxSouthDam.jpg" width="220" height="92" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/6/67/TGDModelAuxSouthDam.jpg/330px-TGDModelAuxSouthDam.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/6/67/TGDModelAuxSouthDam.jpg/440px-TGDModelAuxSouthDam.jpg 2x" data-file-width="512" data-file-height="213" /></a></div>
<div class="thumbcaption" style="clear:left">Earthfill south dam in foreground with view along main dam. The wall beyond is to separate spillway and turbine flows from the lock and ship lift upstream approach channel. A similar separation is used on the downstream side, seen partially in the preceding image.</div>
</div>
</div>
</div>
<p>Made of concrete and steel, the dam is 2,335&#160;m (7,661&#160;ft) long and the top of the dam is 185&#160;m (607&#160;ft) above sea level. The project used 27.2<span style="margin-left:0.2em">×<span style="margin-left:0.1em">10</span></span><s style="display:none">^</s><sup>6</sup>&#160;m<sup>3</sup> (35.6<span style="margin-left:0.2em">×<span style="margin-left:0.1em">10</span></span><s style="display:none">^</s><sup>6</sup>&#160;cu&#160;yd) of concrete (mainly for the dam wall), used 463,000 T of steel (enough to build 63 <a href="/wiki/Eiffel_Tower" title="Eiffel Tower">Eiffel Towers</a>), and moved about 102.6<span style="margin-left:0.2em">×<span style="margin-left:0.1em">10</span></span><s style="display:none">^</s><sup>6</sup>&#160;m<sup>3</sup> (134.2<span style="margin-left:0.2em">×<span style="margin-left:0.1em">10</span></span><s style="display:none">^</s><sup>6</sup>&#160;cu&#160;yd) of earth.<sup id="cite_ref-ibib1_33-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-ibib1-33">[33]</a></sup> The concrete dam wall is 181&#160;m (594&#160;ft) high above the rock basis.</p>
<p>When the water level is at its maximum of 175&#160;m (574&#160;ft) above sea level, 110&#160;m (361&#160;ft) higher than the river level downstream, the dam reservoir is on average about 660&#160;km (410&#160;mi) in length and 1.12&#160;km (3,675&#160;ft) in width. It contains 39.3&#160;km<sup>3</sup> (31,900,000&#160;<a href="/wiki/Acre_foot" class="mw-redirect" title="Acre foot">acre·ft</a>) of water and has a total surface area of 1,045&#160;km<sup>2</sup> (403&#160;sq&#160;mi). On completion, the reservoir flooded a total area of 632&#160;km<sup>2</sup> (244&#160;sq&#160;mi) of land, compared to the 1,350&#160;km<sup>2</sup> (520&#160;sq&#160;mi) of reservoir created by the <a href="/wiki/Itaipu_Dam" title="Itaipu Dam">Itaipu Dam</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-Xinhua20031121_34-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Xinhua20031121-34">[34]</a></sup></p>
<h2><span class="mw-headline" id="Economics">Economics</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Three_Gorges_Dam&amp;action=edit&amp;section=3" title="Edit section: Economics">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h2>
<p>The government estimated that the Three Gorges Dam project would cost 180&#160;billion yuan (US$22.5&#160;billion).<sup id="cite_ref-wpm2007_35-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-wpm2007-35">[35]</a></sup> By the end of 2008, spending had reached 148.365&#160;billion yuan, among which 64.613&#160;billion yuan was spent on construction, 68.557&#160;billion yuan on relocating affected residents, and 15.195&#160;billion yuan on financing.<sup id="cite_ref-36" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-36">[36]</a></sup> It was estimated in 2009 that the construction cost would be recovered when the dam had generated 1,000 terawatt-hours (3,600&#160;PJ) of electricity, yielding 250&#160;billion yuan. Full cost recovery was thus expected to occur ten years after the dam started full operation,<sup id="cite_ref-wpm2007_35-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-wpm2007-35">[35]</a></sup> but the full cost of the Three Gorges Dam was recovered by December 20, 2013.<sup id="cite_ref-37" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-37">[37]</a></sup></p>
<p>Funding sources include the Three Gorges Dam Construction Fund, profits from the <a href="/wiki/Gezhouba_Dam" title="Gezhouba Dam">Gezhouba Dam</a>, loans from the <a href="/wiki/China_Development_Bank" title="China Development Bank">China Development Bank</a>, loans from domestic and foreign commercial banks, <a href="/wiki/Corporate_bond" title="Corporate bond">corporate bonds</a>, and revenue from both before and after the dam is fully operational. Additional charges were assessed as follows: Every province receiving power from the Three Gorges Dam had to pay ¥7.00 per MWh extra. Other provinces had to pay an additional charge of ¥4.00 per MWh. The <a href="/wiki/Tibet_Autonomous_Region" title="Tibet Autonomous Region">Tibet Autonomous Region</a> pays no surcharge.<sup id="cite_ref-38" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-38">[38]</a></sup></p>
<div class="thumb tnone" style="margin-left: auto; margin-right:auto; overflow:hidden; width:auto; max-width:758px;">
<div class="thumbinner" style="">
<div class="overflowbugx" style="overflow:auto;"><a href="/wiki/File:200407-sandouping-sanxiadaba-4.med.jpg" class="image" title="Panorama of the Three Gorges Dam"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/9/95/200407-sandouping-sanxiadaba-4.med.jpg/750px-200407-sandouping-sanxiadaba-4.med.jpg" width="750" height="225" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/9/95/200407-sandouping-sanxiadaba-4.med.jpg/1125px-200407-sandouping-sanxiadaba-4.med.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/9/95/200407-sandouping-sanxiadaba-4.med.jpg/1500px-200407-sandouping-sanxiadaba-4.med.jpg 2x" data-file-width="4096" data-file-height="1228" /></a></div>
<div class="thumbcaption">

<h2><span class="mw-headline" id="Power_generation_and_distribution">Power generation and distribution</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Three_Gorges_Dam&amp;action=edit&amp;section=4" title="Edit section: Power generation and distribution">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h2>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Generating_capacity">Generating capacity</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Three_Gorges_Dam&amp;action=edit&amp;section=5" title="Edit section: Generating capacity">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
<div class="thumb tright">
<div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a href="/wiki/File:Electricity_Production_in_China.svg" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/6/61/Electricity_Production_in_China.svg/220px-Electricity_Production_in_China.svg.png" width="220" height="167" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/6/61/Electricity_Production_in_China.svg/330px-Electricity_Production_in_China.svg.png 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/6/61/Electricity_Production_in_China.svg/440px-Electricity_Production_in_China.svg.png 2x" data-file-width="750" data-file-height="570" /></a>
<div class="thumbcaption">
<div class="magnify"><a href="/wiki/File:Electricity_Production_in_China.svg" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a></div>
Electricity production in China by source. Compare: The fully completed Three Gorges dam will contribute about 100&#160;TWh of generation per year.
<div class="legend"><span class="legend-color" style="display:inline-block; width:1.5em; height:1.5em; margin:1px 0; border:1px solid black; background-color:red; color:black; font-size:100%; text-align:center;">&#160;</span>&#160;thermofossil</div>
<div class="legend"><span class="legend-color" style="display:inline-block; width:1.5em; height:1.5em; margin:1px 0; border:1px solid black; background-color:blue; color:black; font-size:100%; text-align:center;">&#160;</span>&#160;hydroelectric</div>
<div class="legend"><span class="legend-color" style="display:inline-block; width:1.5em; height:1.5em; margin:1px 0; border:1px solid black; background-color:yellow; color:black; font-size:100%; text-align:center;">&#160;</span>&#160;nuclear</div>
</div>
</div>
</div>
<p>Power generation is managed by <a href="/wiki/China_Yangtze_Power" title="China Yangtze Power">China Yangtze Power</a>, a listed subsidiary of <a href="/wiki/China_Three_Gorges_Corporation" title="China Three Gorges Corporation">China Three Gorges Corporation</a> (CTGC) — a Central Enterprise <a href="/wiki/State-owned_enterprise" title="State-owned enterprise">SOE</a> administered by <a href="/wiki/SASAC" class="mw-redirect" title="SASAC">SASAC</a>. The Three Gorges Dam is the world's largest capacity hydroelectric power station with 34&#160;generators: 32 main generators, each with a capacity of 700&#160;MW, and two plant power generators, each with capacity of 50&#160;MW, making a total capacity of 22,500&#160;MW.<sup id="cite_ref-iet2009_13-2" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-iet2009-13">[13]</a></sup> Among those 32 main generators, 14 are installed in the north side of the dam, 12 in the south side, and the remaining six in the <a href="/wiki/Underground_power_station" title="Underground power station">underground power plant</a> in the mountain south of the dam. The expected annual electricity generation will be over 100&#160;TWh.<sup id="cite_ref-39" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-39">[39]</a></sup></p>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Generators">Generators</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Three_Gorges_Dam&amp;action=edit&amp;section=6" title="Edit section: Generators">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
<p>The main generators weigh about 6,000&#160;tonnes each and are designed to produce more than 700&#160;MW of power. The designed <a href="/wiki/Hydraulic_head" title="Hydraulic head">head</a> of the generator is 80.6 meters (264&#160;ft). The flow rate varies between 600–950 cubic metres per second (21,000–34,000&#160;cu&#160;ft/s) depending on the head available. The greater the head, the less water needed to reach full power. Three Gorges uses <a href="/wiki/Francis_turbine" title="Francis turbine">Francis turbines</a>. Turbine diameter is 9.7/10.4&#160;m (VGS design/Alstom's design) and rotation speed is 75&#160;revolutions per minute. Rated power is 778 <a href="/wiki/Volt_ampere" class="mw-redirect" title="Volt ampere">MVA</a>, with a maximum of 840&#160;MVA and a <a href="/wiki/Power_factor" title="Power factor">power factor</a> of 0.9. The generator produces electrical power at 20&#160;<a href="/wiki/Volt" title="Volt">kV</a>. The outer diameter of the generator <a href="/wiki/Stator" title="Stator">stator</a> is 21.4/20.9&#160;m. The inner diameter is 18.5/18.8&#160;m. The stator, the biggest of its kind, is 3.1/3&#160;m in height. Bearing load is 5050/5500 tonnes. Average efficiency is over 94%, and reaches 96.5%.<sup id="cite_ref-40" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-40">[40]</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-41" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-41">[41]</a></sup></p>
<div class="thumb tright">
<div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a href="/wiki/File:Sanxia_Runner04_300.jpg" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/3/32/Sanxia_Runner04_300.jpg/220px-Sanxia_Runner04_300.jpg" width="220" height="165" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/3/32/Sanxia_Runner04_300.jpg/330px-Sanxia_Runner04_300.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/3/32/Sanxia_Runner04_300.jpg/440px-Sanxia_Runner04_300.jpg 2x" data-file-width="1000" data-file-height="750" /></a>
<div class="thumbcaption">
<div class="magnify"><a href="/wiki/File:Sanxia_Runner04_300.jpg" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a></div>
Three Gorges Dam <a href="/wiki/Francis_turbine" title="Francis turbine">Francis turbine</a></div>
</div>
</div>
<p>The generators were manufactured by two joint ventures: one of them <a href="/wiki/Alstom" title="Alstom">Alstom</a>, <a href="/wiki/ABB_Group" title="ABB Group">ABB Group</a>, <a href="/wiki/Kvaerner" class="mw-redirect" title="Kvaerner">Kvaerner</a>, and the Chinese company Haerbin Motor; the other <a href="/wiki/Voith" title="Voith">Voith</a>, <a href="/wiki/General_Electric" title="General Electric">General Electric</a>, <a href="/wiki/Siemens" title="Siemens">Siemens</a> (abbreviated as VGS), and the Chinese company Oriental Motor. The technology transfer agreement was signed together with the contract. Most of the generators are water-cooled. Some newer ones are air-cooled, which are simpler in design and manufacture and are easier to maintain.<sup id="cite_ref-Chinacom20020726_42-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Chinacom20020726-42">[42]</a></sup></p>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Generator_installation_progress">Generator installation progress</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Three_Gorges_Dam&amp;action=edit&amp;section=7" title="Edit section: Generator installation progress">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
<p>The 14 north side main generators are in operation. The first (No.&#160;2) started on July 10, 2003. The north side became completely operational September 7, 2005 with the implementation of generator No.&#160;9. Full power (9,800&#160;MW) was only reached on October 18, 2006 after the water level reached 156&#160;m.<sup id="cite_ref-43" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-43">[43]</a></sup></p>
<p>The 12 south side main generators are also in operation. No.&#160;22 began operation on June 11, 2007 and No.&#160;15 started up on October 30, 2008.<sup id="cite_ref-ctgpc1_14-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-ctgpc1-14">[14]</a></sup> The sixth (No.&#160;17) began operation on December 18, 2007, raising capacity to 14.1&#160;GW, finally surpassing <a href="/wiki/Itaipu_Dam" title="Itaipu Dam">Itaipu</a> (14.0&#160;GW), to become the world's largest hydro power plant by capacity.<sup id="cite_ref-Ctgpc20080505_44-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Ctgpc20080505-44">[44]</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-45" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-45">[45]</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-46" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-46">[46]</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-47" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-47">[47]</a></sup></p>
<p>As of May 23, 2012 when the last main generator, No. 27, finished its final test, the six underground main generators are also in operation, raising capacity to 22.5 GW.<sup id="cite_ref-autogenerated5_10-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-autogenerated5-10">[10]</a></sup> After nine years of construction, installation and testing, the power plant is now fully operational.<sup id="cite_ref-inventspot_16-2" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-inventspot-16">[16]</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-48" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-48">[48]</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-49" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-49">[49]</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-50" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-50">[50]</a></sup></p>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Output_milestones">Output milestones</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Three_Gorges_Dam&amp;action=edit&amp;section=8" title="Edit section: Output milestones">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
<div class="thumb tright">
<div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a href="/wiki/File:Three_gorges_dam_annual_power_output.JPG" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/d/d8/Three_gorges_dam_annual_power_output.JPG/220px-Three_gorges_dam_annual_power_output.JPG" width="220" height="165" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/d/d8/Three_gorges_dam_annual_power_output.JPG/330px-Three_gorges_dam_annual_power_output.JPG 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/d/d8/Three_gorges_dam_annual_power_output.JPG/440px-Three_gorges_dam_annual_power_output.JPG 2x" data-file-width="651" data-file-height="487" /></a>
<div class="thumbcaption">
<div class="magnify"><a href="/wiki/File:Three_gorges_dam_annual_power_output.JPG" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a></div>
Three Gorges Dam annual power output</div>
</div>
</div>
<div class="thumb tright">
<div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a href="/wiki/File:Yangtze_River_flow_rate_at_TGD_site.JPG" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/3/3a/Yangtze_River_flow_rate_at_TGD_site.JPG/220px-Yangtze_River_flow_rate_at_TGD_site.JPG" width="220" height="150" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/3/3a/Yangtze_River_flow_rate_at_TGD_site.JPG/330px-Yangtze_River_flow_rate_at_TGD_site.JPG 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/3/3a/Yangtze_River_flow_rate_at_TGD_site.JPG/440px-Yangtze_River_flow_rate_at_TGD_site.JPG 2x" data-file-width="699" data-file-height="476" /></a>
<div class="thumbcaption">
<div class="magnify"><a href="/wiki/File:Yangtze_River_flow_rate_at_TGD_site.JPG" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a></div>
Yangtze River flow rate comparing to the dam intake capacity</div>
</div>
</div>
<p>By August 16, 2011, the plant had generated 500&#160;TWh of electricity.<sup id="cite_ref-51" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-51">[51]</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-52" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-52">[52]</a></sup> In July 2008 it generated 10.3&#160;TWh of electricity, its first month over 10&#160;TWh.<sup id="cite_ref-53" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-53">[53]</a></sup> On June 30, 2009, after the river flow rate increased to over 24,000&#160;m<sup>3</sup>, all 28 generators were switched on, producing only 16,100&#160;MW because the head available during flood season is insufficient.<sup id="cite_ref-54" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-54">[54]</a></sup> During an August 2009 flood, the plant first reached its maximum output for a short period.<sup id="cite_ref-ctgpc2_55-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-ctgpc2-55">[55]</a></sup></p>
<p>During the November to May dry season, power output is limited by the river's flow rate, as seen in the diagrams on the right. When there is enough flow, power output is limited by plant generating capacity. The maximum power-output curves were calculated based on the average flow rate at the dam site, assuming the water level is 175&#160;m and the plant gross efficiency is 90.15%. The actual power output in 2008 was obtained based on the monthly electricity sent to the grid.<sup id="cite_ref-56" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-56">[56]</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-57" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-57">[57]</a></sup></p>
<p>The Three Gorges Dam reached its design-maximum reservoir water level of 175&#160;m (574&#160;ft) for the first time on October 26, 2010, in which the intended annual power-generation capacity of 84.7 TWh was realized.<sup id="cite_ref-Xin2010_31-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Xin2010-31">[31]</a></sup> In 2012, the dam's 32 generating units generated a record 98.1 TWh of electricity, which accounts for 14% of China's total hydro generation.<sup id="cite_ref-58" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-58">[58]</a></sup></p>

<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Distribution">Distribution</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Three_Gorges_Dam&amp;action=edit&amp;section=9" title="Edit section: Distribution">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
<p>The <a href="/wiki/State_Grid_Corporation" class="mw-redirect" title="State Grid Corporation">State Grid Corporation</a> and <a href="/wiki/China_Southern_Power_Grid" title="China Southern Power Grid">China Southern Power Grid</a> paid a flat rate of ¥250&#160;per MWh (US$35.7) until July 2, 2008. Since then, the price has varied by province, from ¥228.7–401.8&#160;per MWh. Higher-paying customers receive priority, such as <a href="/wiki/Shanghai" title="Shanghai">Shanghai</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-67" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-67">[67]</a></sup> Nine provinces and two cities consume power from the dam.<sup id="cite_ref-chinagate_68-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-chinagate-68">[68]</a></sup></p>
<p>Power distribution and transmission infrastructure cost about 34.387&#160;billion Yuan. Construction was completed in December 2007, one year ahead of schedule.<sup id="cite_ref-69" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-69">[69]</a></sup></p>
<p>Power is distributed over multiple 500 <a href="/wiki/Kilovolt" class="mw-redirect" title="Kilovolt">kilovolt</a> (kV) transmission lines. Three <a href="/wiki/Direct_current" title="Direct current">direct current</a> (DC) lines to the East China Grid carry 7,200 MW: Three Gorges – Shanghai (3,000 MW), <a href="/wiki/HVDC_Three_Gorges_%E2%80%93_Changzhou" title="HVDC Three Gorges – Changzhou">HVDC Three Gorges – Changzhou</a> (3,000 MW), and <a href="/wiki/HVDC_Gezhouba_%E2%80%93_Shanghai" class="mw-redirect" title="HVDC Gezhouba – Shanghai">HVDC Gezhouba – Shanghai</a> (1,200 MW). The <a href="/wiki/Alternating_current" title="Alternating current">alternating current</a> (AC) lines to the Central China Grid have a total capacity of 12,000 MW. The DC transmission line <a href="/wiki/HVDC_Three_Gorges_%E2%80%93_Guangdong" title="HVDC Three Gorges – Guangdong">HVDC Three Gorges – Guangdong</a> to the South China Grid has a capacity of 3,000 MW.<sup id="cite_ref-abb_70-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-abb-70">[70]</a></sup></p>
<p>The dam was expected to provide 10% of China's power. However, electricity demand has increased more quickly than previously projected. Even fully operational, on average, it supports only about 1.7% of electricity demand in China in the year of 2011, when the Chinese electricity demand reached 4692.8 TWh.<sup id="cite_ref-71" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-71">[71]</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-72" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-72">[72]</a></sup></p>
<h2><span class="mw-headline" id="Environmental_impact">Environmental impact</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Three_Gorges_Dam&amp;action=edit&amp;section=10" title="Edit section: Environmental impact">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h2>
<div class="thumb tright">
<div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a href="/wiki/File:ThreeGorgesDam-Landsat7.jpg" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/a/a8/ThreeGorgesDam-Landsat7.jpg/220px-ThreeGorgesDam-Landsat7.jpg" width="220" height="287" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/a/a8/ThreeGorgesDam-Landsat7.jpg/330px-ThreeGorgesDam-Landsat7.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/a/a8/ThreeGorgesDam-Landsat7.jpg/440px-ThreeGorgesDam-Landsat7.jpg 2x" data-file-width="540" data-file-height="705" /></a>

</div>
</div>
<div class="thumb tright">
