Flood mark on Yangtze river</div>
</div>
</div>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Emissions">Emissions</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Three_Gorges_Dam&amp;action=edit&amp;section=11" title="Edit section: Emissions">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
<p>According to the National Development and Reform Commission of China, 366&#160;grams of coal would produce 1&#160;kWh of electricity during 2006.<sup id="cite_ref-73" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-73">[73]</a></sup> At full power, Three Gorges reduces coal consumption by 31&#160;million tonnes per year, avoiding 100&#160;million tonnes of greenhouse gas emissions,<sup id="cite_ref-74" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-74">[74]</a></sup> millions of tonnes of dust, one&#160;million tonnes of <a href="/wiki/Sulfur_dioxide" title="Sulfur dioxide">sulfur dioxide</a>, 370,000&#160;tonnes of <a href="/wiki/Nitric_oxide" title="Nitric oxide">nitric oxide</a>, 10,000&#160;tonnes of <a href="/wiki/Carbon_monoxide" title="Carbon monoxide">carbon monoxide</a>, and a significant amount of <a href="/wiki/Mercury_(element)" title="Mercury (element)">mercury</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-75" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-75">[75]</a></sup> Hydropower saves the energy needed to mine, wash, and transport the coal from northern China.</p>
<p>From 2003 to 2007, power production equaled that of 84&#160;million tonnes of standard coal, reducing carbon dioxide by 190&#160;million tonnes, sulfur dioxide by 2.29&#160;million tonnes, and nitrogen oxides by 980,000&#160;tonnes.<sup id="cite_ref-Xinhuar2007023_76-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Xinhuar2007023-76">[76]</a></sup></p>
<p>The dam increased the Yangtze's barge capacity sixfold, reducing carbon dioxide emission by 630,000&#160;tonnes. From 2004 to 2007 a total of 198 million tonnes of goods passed through the ship locks. Compared to using trucking, barges reduced carbon dioxide emission by ten&#160;million tonnes and lowered costs by 25%.<sup id="cite_ref-Xinhuar2007023_76-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Xinhuar2007023-76">[76]</a></sup></p>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Erosion_and_sedimentation">Erosion and sedimentation</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Three_Gorges_Dam&amp;action=edit&amp;section=12" title="Edit section: Erosion and sedimentation">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
<p>Two hazards are uniquely identified with the dam.<sup id="cite_ref-77" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-77">[77]</a></sup> One is that sedimentation projections are not agreed upon, and the other is that the dam sits on a seismic fault. At current levels, 80% of the land in the area is experiencing erosion, depositing about 40&#160;million tons of <a href="/wiki/Sediment" title="Sediment">sediment</a> into the <a href="/wiki/Yangtze" title="Yangtze">Yangtze</a> annually.<sup id="cite_ref-autogenerated1_78-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-autogenerated1-78">[78]</a></sup> Because the flow is slower above the dam, much of this sediment will now settle there instead of flowing downstream, and there will be less sediment downstream.</p>
<p>The absence of <a href="/wiki/Silt" title="Silt">silt</a> downstream has three effects:</p>
<ul>
<li>Some hydrologists expect downstream riverbanks to become more vulnerable to flooding.<sup id="cite_ref-79" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-79">[79]</a></sup></li>
<li>Shanghai, more than 1,600&#160;km (990&#160;mi) away, rests on a massive sedimentary plain. The "arriving silt—so long as it does arrive—strengthens the bed on which Shanghai is built... the less the tonnage of arriving sediment the more vulnerable is this biggest of Chinese cities to inundation..."<sup id="cite_ref-80" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-80">[80]</a></sup></li>
<li><a href="/wiki/Benthic_zone" title="Benthic zone">Benthic</a> sediment buildup causes biological damage and reduces aquatic <a href="/wiki/Biodiversity" title="Biodiversity">biodiversity</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-81" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-81">[81]</a></sup></li>
</ul>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Earthquakes_and_landslides">Earthquakes and landslides</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Three_Gorges_Dam&amp;action=edit&amp;section=13" title="Edit section: Earthquakes and landslides">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
<p>Erosion in the reservoir, induced by rising water, causes frequent major <a href="/wiki/Landslide" title="Landslide">landslides</a> that have led to noticeable disturbance in the reservoir surface, including two incidents in May 2009 when somewhere between 20,000 and 50,000 cubic metres (26,000 and 65,000&#160;cu&#160;yd) of material plunged into the flooded Wuxia Gorge of the <a href="/wiki/Wu_River_(Yangtze_River)" class="mw-redirect" title="Wu River (Yangtze River)">Wu River</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-82" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-82">[82]</a></sup> Also, in the first four months of 2010, there were 97 significant landslides.<sup id="cite_ref-landslides_83-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-landslides-83">[83]</a></sup></p>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Waste_management">Waste management</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Three_Gorges_Dam&amp;action=edit&amp;section=14" title="Edit section: Waste management">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
<div class="thumb tright">
<div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a href="/wiki/File:Maoping-Drinking-water-source-protection-area-4937.JPG" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/d/d8/Maoping-Drinking-water-source-protection-area-4937.JPG/220px-Maoping-Drinking-water-source-protection-area-4937.JPG" width="220" height="165" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/d/d8/Maoping-Drinking-water-source-protection-area-4937.JPG/330px-Maoping-Drinking-water-source-protection-area-4937.JPG 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/d/d8/Maoping-Drinking-water-source-protection-area-4937.JPG/440px-Maoping-Drinking-water-source-protection-area-4937.JPG 2x" data-file-width="2048" data-file-height="1536" /></a>
<div class="thumbcaption">
<div class="magnify"><a href="/wiki/File:Maoping-Drinking-water-source-protection-area-4937.JPG" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a></div>
<a href="/wiki/Zigui_County" title="Zigui County">Zigui County</a> seat <a href="/wiki/Source_water_protection" title="Source water protection">source water protection</a> area in <a href="/wiki/Maoping,_Hubei" title="Maoping, Hubei">Maoping Town</a>, a few kilometers upstream of the dam</div>
</div>
</div>
<p>The dam catalyzed improved upstream <a href="/wiki/Wastewater" title="Wastewater">wastewater</a> treatment around <a href="/wiki/Chongqing" title="Chongqing">Chongqing</a> and its suburban areas. According to the Ministry of Environmental Protection, as of April 2007 more than 50 new plants could treat 1.84&#160;million tonnes per day, 65% of the total need. About 32 landfills were added, which could handle 7,664.5&#160;tonnes of solid waste every day.<sup id="cite_ref-Xinhua20080503_84-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Xinhua20080503-84">[84]</a></sup> Over one&#160;billion tons of wastewater are released annually into the river,<sup id="cite_ref-autogenerated1_78-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-autogenerated1-78">[78]</a></sup> which was more likely to be swept away before the reservoir was created. This has left the water looking stagnant, polluted and murky.<sup id="cite_ref-landslides_83-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-landslides-83">[83]</a></sup></p>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Forest_cover">Forest cover</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Three_Gorges_Dam&amp;action=edit&amp;section=15" title="Edit section: Forest cover">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
<p>In 1997 the Three Gorges area had 10% forestation, down from 20% in the 1950s.<sup id="cite_ref-autogenerated1_78-2" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-autogenerated1-78">[78]</a></sup></p>
<p>Research by the <a href="/wiki/United_Nations" title="United Nations">United Nations</a> <a href="/wiki/Food_and_Agriculture_Organization" title="Food and Agriculture Organization">Food and Agriculture Organization</a> research suggested that the Asia-Pacific region would, overall, gain about 6,000&#160;km<sup>2</sup> (2,300&#160;sq&#160;mi) of forest by 2008. That is a significant change from the 13,000&#160;km<sup>2</sup> (5,000&#160;sq&#160;mi) net loss of forest each year in the 1990s. The main reason is China's huge reforestation effort. This accelerated after the <a href="/wiki/1998_Yangtze_River_floods" class="mw-redirect" title="1998 Yangtze River floods">1998 Yangtze River floods</a> convinced the government that it must restore tree cover, especially in the Yangtze's basin upstream of the Three Gorges Dam.<sup id="cite_ref-85" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-85">[85]</a></sup></p>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Wildlife">Wildlife</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Three_Gorges_Dam&amp;action=edit&amp;section=16" title="Edit section: Wildlife">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
<p>Concerns about the potential wildlife impact of the dam predate the <a href="/wiki/National_People%27s_Congress" title="National People's Congress">National People's Congress</a>'s approval in 1992.<sup id="cite_ref-Li_86-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Li-86">[86]</a></sup> This region has long been known for its rich biodiversity. It is home to 6,388 species of plants, which belong to 238 families and 1508 genera. Of these plant species, 57 percent are endangered.<sup id="cite_ref-Wu_Jianguo_87-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Wu_Jianguo-87">[87]</a></sup> These rare species are also used as ingredients in traditional Chinese medicines.<sup id="cite_ref-88" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-88">[88]</a></sup> Already, the percentage of forested area in the region surrounding the Three Gorges Dam has dropped from twenty percent in 1950 to less than ten percent as of 2002,<sup id="cite_ref-89" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-89">[89]</a></sup> negatively affecting all plant species in this locality. The region also provides habitats to hundreds of freshwater and terrestrial animal species.<sup id="cite_ref-Wu_Jianguo_87-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Wu_Jianguo-87">[87]</a></sup> Freshwater fish are especially affected by dams due to changes in the water temperature and flow regime. Many other fish are hurt in the turbine blades of the hydroelectric plants as well. This is particularly detrimental to the ecosystem of the region because the Yangtze River basin is home to 361 different fish species and accounts for twenty-seven percent of all endangered freshwater fish species in China.<sup id="cite_ref-90" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-90">[90]</a></sup> Other aquatic species have been endangered by the dam, particularly the baiji, or <a href="/wiki/Chinese_river_dolphin" class="mw-redirect" title="Chinese river dolphin">Chinese river dolphin</a>,<sup id="cite_ref-autogenerated1_78-3" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-autogenerated1-78">[78]</a></sup> now extinct. In fact, Government Chinese scholars even claim that the Three Gorges Dam directly caused the extinction of the baiji.<sup id="cite_ref-TheAge_101307_91-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-TheAge_101307-91">[91]</a></sup></p>
<p>Of the 3,000 to 4,000 remaining <a href="/wiki/Critically_endangered" title="Critically endangered">critically endangered</a> <a href="/wiki/Siberian_crane" title="Siberian crane">Siberian crane</a>, a large number currently spend the winter in wetlands that will be destroyed by the Three Gorges Dam.<sup id="cite_ref-92" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-92">[92]</a></sup> The dam contributed to the <a href="/wiki/Functional_extinction" title="Functional extinction">functional extinction</a> of the <a href="/wiki/Baiji" title="Baiji">baiji</a> Yangtze river dolphin. Though it was close to this level even at the start of construction, the dam further decreased its habitat and increased ship travel, which are among the factors causing what will be its ultimate demise. In addition, populations of the <a href="/wiki/Yangtze_sturgeon" class="mw-redirect" title="Yangtze sturgeon">Yangtze sturgeon</a> are guaranteed to be "negatively affected" by the dam.<sup id="cite_ref-93" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-93">[93]</a></sup></p>
<h2><span class="mw-headline" id="Floods.2C_agriculture.2C_industry">Floods, agriculture, industry</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Three_Gorges_Dam&amp;action=edit&amp;section=17" title="Edit section: Floods, agriculture, industry">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h2>
<p>An important function of the dam is to control flooding, which is a major problem for the seasonal river of the Yangtze. Millions of people live downstream of the dam, with many large, important cities like <a href="/wiki/Wuhan" title="Wuhan">Wuhan</a>, <a href="/wiki/Nanjing" title="Nanjing">Nanjing</a>, and Shanghai situated adjacent to the river. Plenty of farm land and China's most important industrial area are built beside the river.</p>
<p>The reservoir's flood storage capacity is 22 cubic kilometres (18,000,000&#160;<a href="/wiki/Acre_foot" class="mw-redirect" title="Acre foot">acre·ft</a>). This capacity will reduce the frequency of major downstream flooding from once every ten years to once every 100&#160;years. The dam is expected to minimize the effect of even a "super" flood.<sup id="cite_ref-94" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-94">[94]</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-95" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-95">[95]</a></sup> <a href="/wiki/1954_Yangtze_River_Floods" class="mw-redirect" title="1954 Yangtze River Floods">In 1954 the river flooded</a> 193,000&#160;km<sup>2</sup> (74,518&#160;sq&#160;mi), killing 33,169&#160;people and forcing 18,884,000&#160;people to move. The flood covered Wuhan, a city of eight million people, for over three months, and the <a href="/wiki/Jingguang_Railway" class="mw-redirect" title="Jingguang Railway">Jingguang Railway</a> was out of service for more than 100&#160;days.<sup id="cite_ref-96" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-96">[96]</a></sup> The 1954 flood carried 50 cubic kilometres (12&#160;cu&#160;mi) of water. The dam could only divert the water above Chenglingji, leaving 30 to 40&#160;km<sup>3</sup> (7.2 to 9.6&#160;cu&#160;mi) to be diverted.<sup id="cite_ref-97" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-97">[97]</a></sup> Also the dam cannot protect against some of the large tributaries downstream, including the <a href="/wiki/Xiang_River" title="Xiang River">Xiang</a>, <a href="/wiki/Zi_River" title="Zi River">Zishui</a>, <a href="/wiki/Yuan_River" title="Yuan River">Yuanshui</a>, <a href="/wiki/Lishui_River" title="Lishui River">Lishui</a>, <a href="/wiki/Han_River_(Hanshui)" class="mw-redirect" title="Han River (Hanshui)">Hanshui</a>, and the <a href="/wiki/Gan_River_(Jiangxi)" class="mw-redirect" title="Gan River (Jiangxi)">Gan</a>.</p>
<p><a href="/wiki/1998_Yangtze_River_Floods" class="mw-redirect" title="1998 Yangtze River Floods">In 1998 a flood in the same area</a> caused billions of dollars in damage; 2,039&#160;km<sup>2</sup> (787&#160;sq&#160;mi) of farm land were flooded. The flood affected more than 2.3&#160;million people, killing 1,526.<sup id="cite_ref-98" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-98">[98]</a></sup> In early August 2009, the largest flood in five years passed through the dam site. The dam limited the water flow to less than 40,000 cubic metres (52,000&#160;cu&#160;yd) per second, raising the upstream water level from 145.13&#160;metres on August 1, 2009, to 152.88 on August 8, 2009. 4.27 cubic kilometres of flood water were captured and the river flow was cut by as much as 15,000 cubic metres per second.<sup id="cite_ref-ctgpc2_55-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-ctgpc2-55">[55]</a></sup></p>
<p>The dam discharges its reservoir during the dry season between December and March every year.<sup id="cite_ref-99" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-99">[99]</a></sup> This increases the flow rate of the river downstream, and provides fresh water for agricultural and industrial usage. It also improves shipping conditions. The water level upstream drops from 175&#160;m to 145&#160;m,<sup id="cite_ref-100" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-100">[100]</a></sup> preparing for the rainy season. The water also powers the Gezhouba Dam downstream.</p>
<p>Since the filling of the reservoir in 2003, the Three Gorges Dam has supplied an extra 11&#160;cubic kilometres of fresh water to downstream cities and farms during the dry season.<sup id="cite_ref-101" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-101">[101]</a></sup> <span id="Navigation"></span></p>
<p>During the <a href="/wiki/2010_South_China_floods" class="mw-redirect" title="2010 South China floods">2010 South China floods</a>, in July, inflows at the Three Gorges Dam reached a peak of 70,000&#160;m<sup>3</sup>/s (2,500,000&#160;cu&#160;ft/s), exceeding the peak during the <a href="/wiki/1998_Yangtze_River_Floods" class="mw-redirect" title="1998 Yangtze River Floods">1998 Yangtze River Floods</a>. The dam's reservoir rose nearly 3&#160;m (9.8&#160;ft) in 24 hours and reduced the outflow to 40,000&#160;m<sup>3</sup>/s (1,400,000&#160;cu&#160;ft/s) in discharges downstream, effectively alleviating serious impacts on the middle and lower river.<sup id="cite_ref-102" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-102">[102]</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-103" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-103">[103]</a></sup></p>
<h2><span class="mw-headline" id="Navigating_the_dam">Navigating the dam</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Three_Gorges_Dam&amp;action=edit&amp;section=18" title="Edit section: Navigating the dam">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h2>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Locks">Locks</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Three_Gorges_Dam&amp;action=edit&amp;section=19" title="Edit section: Locks">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
<div class="thumb tright">
<div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a href="/wiki/File:Three_gorges_dam_locks_view_from_vantage_point.jpg" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/8/83/Three_gorges_dam_locks_view_from_vantage_point.jpg/220px-Three_gorges_dam_locks_view_from_vantage_point.jpg" width="220" height="165" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/8/83/Three_gorges_dam_locks_view_from_vantage_point.jpg/330px-Three_gorges_dam_locks_view_from_vantage_point.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/8/83/Three_gorges_dam_locks_view_from_vantage_point.jpg/440px-Three_gorges_dam_locks_view_from_vantage_point.jpg 2x" data-file-width="1024" data-file-height="768" /></a>
<div class="thumbcaption">
<div class="magnify"><a href="/wiki/File:Three_gorges_dam_locks_view_from_vantage_point.jpg" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a></div>
<a href="/wiki/Lock_(water_transport)" class="mw-redirect" title="Lock (water transport)">Ship locks</a> for river traffic to bypass the Three Gorges Dam, May 2004</div>
</div>
</div>
<div class="thumb tright">
<div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a href="/wiki/File:Three_Gorges_dam_locks_and_bridge.jpg" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/f/fd/Three_Gorges_dam_locks_and_bridge.jpg/220px-Three_Gorges_dam_locks_and_bridge.jpg" width="220" height="165" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/f/fd/Three_Gorges_dam_locks_and_bridge.jpg/330px-Three_Gorges_dam_locks_and_bridge.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/f/fd/Three_Gorges_dam_locks_and_bridge.jpg/440px-Three_Gorges_dam_locks_and_bridge.jpg 2x" data-file-width="3264" data-file-height="2448" /></a>
<div class="thumbcaption">
<div class="magnify"><a href="/wiki/File:Three_Gorges_dam_locks_and_bridge.jpg" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a></div>
The other end of Three gorges dam lock, note the Bridge in the background</div>
</div>
</div>
<p>The installation of <a href="/wiki/Lock_(water_transport)" class="mw-redirect" title="Lock (water transport)">ship locks</a> is intended to increase river shipping from ten&#160;million to 100&#160;million tonnes annually, as a result transportation costs will be cut between 30 and 37%. Shipping will become safer, since the gorges are notoriously dangerous to navigate.<sup id="cite_ref-Xinhuar2007023_76-2" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Xinhuar2007023-76">[76]</a></sup> Ships with much deeper draft will be able to navigate 2,400 kilometres (1,500&#160;mi) upstream from Shanghai all the way to <a href="/wiki/Chongqing" title="Chongqing">Chongqing</a>. It is expected that shipping to Chongqing will increase fivefold.<sup id="cite_ref-104" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-104">[104]</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-WashingtonPost_105-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-WashingtonPost-105">[105]</a></sup></p>
<p>There are two series of ship locks installed near the dam (<span class="plainlinks nourlexpansion"><a class="external text" href="//tools.wmflabs.org/geohack/geohack.php?pagename=Three_Gorges_Dam&amp;params=30_50_12_N_111_1_10_E_region:CN-62_type:landmark"><span class="geo-default"><span class="geo-dms" title="Maps, aerial photos, and other data for this location"><span class="latitude">30°50′12″N</span> <span class="longitude">111°1′10″E</span></span></span><span class="geo-multi-punct">﻿ / ﻿</span><span class="geo-nondefault"><span class="geo-dec" title="Maps, aerial photos, and other data for this location">30.83667°N 111.01944°E</span><span style="display:none">﻿ / <span class="geo">30.83667; 111.01944</span></span></span></a></span>). Each of them is made up of five stages, with transit time at around four hours. Maximum vessel size is 10,000&#160;tons.<sup id="cite_ref-106" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-106">[106]</a></sup> The locks are 280&#160;m long, 35&#160;m wide, and 5&#160;m deep (918 × 114 × 16.4&#160;ft).<sup id="cite_ref-Moafs20020420_107-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Moafs20020420-107">[107]</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-108" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-108">[108]</a></sup> That is 30&#160;m longer than those on the <a href="/wiki/St_Lawrence_Seaway" class="mw-redirect" title="St Lawrence Seaway">St Lawrence Seaway</a>, but half as deep. Before the dam was constructed, the maximum freight capacity at the Three Gorges site was 18.0&#160;million tonnes per year. From 2004 to 2007, a total of 198&#160;million tonnes of freight passed through the locks. The freight capacity of the river increased six&#160;times and the cost of shipping was reduced by 25%. The total capacity of the ship locks is expected to reach 100&#160;million tonnes per year.<sup id="cite_ref-Xinhuar2007023_76-3" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Xinhuar2007023-76">[76]</a></sup></p>
<p>These locks are <a href="/wiki/Lock_gates#Special_cases" class="mw-redirect" title="Lock gates">staircase locks</a>, whereby inner lock gate pairs serve as both the upper gate and lower gate. The <a href="/wiki/Lock_gates#Variations" class="mw-redirect" title="Lock gates">gates</a> are the vulnerable hinged type, which, if damaged, could temporarily render the entire flight unusable. As there are separate sets of locks for upstream and downstream traffic, this system is more water efficient than bi-directional staircase locks.</p>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Ship_lift">Ship lift</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Three_Gorges_Dam&amp;action=edit&amp;section=20" title="Edit section: Ship lift">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
<div class="thumb tright">
<div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a href="/wiki/File:Three_Gorges_Dam_(12280456164).jpg" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/0/02/Three_Gorges_Dam_%2812280456164%29.jpg/220px-Three_Gorges_Dam_%2812280456164%29.jpg" width="220" height="165" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/0/02/Three_Gorges_Dam_%2812280456164%29.jpg/330px-Three_Gorges_Dam_%2812280456164%29.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/0/02/Three_Gorges_Dam_%2812280456164%29.jpg/440px-Three_Gorges_Dam_%2812280456164%29.jpg 2x" data-file-width="2816" data-file-height="2112" /></a>
<div class="thumbcaption">
<div class="magnify"><a href="/wiki/File:Three_Gorges_Dam_(12280456164).jpg" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a></div>
The <i>shiplift</i>, a kind of elevator, can lift vessels of up to 3,000 tonnes, at a fraction of the time to transit the staircase locks.</div>
</div>
</div>
<p>In addition to the canal locks, there is a <a href="/wiki/Boat_lift" title="Boat lift">ship lift</a>, a kind of elevator for vessels. The ship lift can lift ships of up to 3,000&#160;tons.<sup id="cite_ref-shipcom_12-2" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-shipcom-12">[12]</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-Bbc2005050_109-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Bbc2005050-109">[109]</a></sup> The vertical distance traveled is 113 metres,<sup id="cite_ref-ChinaThreeGorgesProject_110-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-ChinaThreeGorgesProject-110">[110]</a></sup> and the size of the ship lift's basin is 120×18×3.5 metres. The ship lift takes 30 to 40 minutes to transit, as opposed to the three to four hours for stepping through the locks.<sup id="cite_ref-Bbc050504_111-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Bbc050504-111">[111]</a></sup> One complicating factor is that the water level can vary dramatically. The ship lift must work even if water levels vary by 12 meters (39&#160;ft) on the lower side, and 30&#160;metres on the upper side.</p>
<p>The ship lift's design uses a helical gear system, to climb or descend a toothed rack.<sup id="cite_ref-Lahmeyer2013_112-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Lahmeyer2013-112">[112]</a></sup></p>
<p>The ship lift was not yet complete when the rest of the project was officially opened on May 20, 2006.<sup id="cite_ref-TaipeiTimes20080521_113-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-TaipeiTimes20080521-113">[113]</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-CbsNews20060520_114-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-CbsNews20060520-114">[114]</a></sup> In November 2007 it was reported in the local media that construction of the ship lift started in October 2007.<sup id="cite_ref-CnHubei20071110_30-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-CnHubei20071110-30">[30]</a></sup></p>
<p>In February 2012 <i><a href="/wiki/Xinhua" class="mw-redirect" title="Xinhua">Xinhua</a></i> reported that the four towers that are to support the ship lift had almost been completed.<sup id="cite_ref-Xinhua2012-02-27_115-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Xinhua2012-02-27-115">[115]</a></sup></p>
<p>The report said the towers had reached 189 metres of the anticipated 195 metres, the towers would be completed by June 2012 and the entire shiplift in 2015.</p>
<p>As of May 2014, the ship lift was expected to be completed by July 2015.<sup id="cite_ref-116" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-116">[116]</a></sup> It was tested in December 2015 and announced complete in January 2016.<sup id="cite_ref-shipcom_12-3" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-shipcom-12">[12]</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-ChinaEconomicNet2016-02-17_117-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-ChinaEconomicNet2016-02-17-117">[117]</a></sup> <a href="/w/index.php?title=Lahmeyer&amp;action=edit&amp;redlink=1" class="new" title="Lahmeyer (page does not exist)">Lahmeyer</a>, the German firm that designed the ship lift, said it will take a vessel less than an hour to transit the lift.<sup id="cite_ref-Lahmeyer2013_112-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Lahmeyer2013-112">[112]</a></sup> An article in Steel Construction says the actual time of the lift will be 21 minutes.<sup id="cite_ref-SteelConstruction2009_118-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-SteelConstruction2009-118">[118]</a></sup> It says that the expected dimensions of the 3,000 tonnes (3,000,000&#160;kg) passenger vessels the ship lift's basin was designed to carry will be 84.5 metres (277&#160;ft) X 17.2 metres (56&#160;ft) X 2.65 metres (8.7&#160;ft).</p>
<p>The trials of elevator finished in July 2016, the first cargo ship was lifted in July 15, the lift time comprised 8 minutes.<sup id="cite_ref-slt1_119-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-slt1-119">[119]</a></sup> <i><a href="/wiki/Shanghai_Daily" title="Shanghai Daily">Shanghai Daily</a></i> reported that the first operational use of the lift was on September 18, 2016, when limited <i>"operational testing"</i> of the lift began.<sup id="cite_ref-ShanghaiDaily2016-09-18_120-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-ShanghaiDaily2016-09-18-120">[120]</a></sup></p>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Portage_railways">Portage railways</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Three_Gorges_Dam&amp;action=edit&amp;section=21" title="Edit section: Portage railways">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
<p>Plans also exist for the construction of short <a href="/wiki/Portage_railway" title="Portage railway">portage railways</a> bypassing the dam area altogether. Two short rail lines, one on each side of the river, are to be constructed. The 88 kilometer long northern portage railway (北岸翻坝铁路) will run from the <a href="/wiki/Taipingxi" title="Taipingxi">Taipingxi</a> port facility (太平溪港) on the northern side of the Yangtze, just upstream from the dam, via <a href="/wiki/Yichang_East_Railway_Station" title="Yichang East Railway Station">Yichang East Railway Station</a> to the Baiyang Tianjiahe port facility in Baiyang Town (<a href="https://zh.wikipedia.org/wiki/%E7%99%BD%E6%B4%8B%E9%95%87" class="extiw" title="zh:白洋镇">白洋镇</a>), below Yichang.<sup id="cite_ref-mayor_121-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-mayor-121">[121]</a></sup> The 95 kilometer long southern portage railway (南岸翻坝铁路) will run from <a href="/wiki/Maoping,_Hubei" title="Maoping, Hubei">Maoping</a> (upstream of the dam) via <a href="/wiki/Yichang_South_Railway_Station" title="Yichang South Railway Station">Yichang South Railway Station</a> to <a href="/wiki/Zhicheng" title="Zhicheng">Zhicheng</a> (on the <a href="/wiki/Jiaozuo%E2%80%93Liuzhou_Railway" title="Jiaozuo–Liuzhou Railway">Jiaozuo–Liuzhou Railway</a>).<sup id="cite_ref-mayor_121-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-mayor-121">[121]</a></sup></p>
<p>In late 2012, preliminary work started along both future railway routes.<sup id="cite_ref-Qq2012-10-12_122-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Qq2012-10-12-122">[122]</a></sup></p>
<h2><span class="mw-headline" id="Relocation_of_residents">Relocation of residents</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Three_Gorges_Dam&amp;action=edit&amp;section=22" title="Edit section: Relocation of residents">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h2>
<p>The great size of the reservoir and the huge relocation it caused was justified by the flood protection it provides for communities downstream.<sup id="cite_ref-123" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-123">[123]</a></sup> As of June 2008, China relocated 1.24&#160;million residents (ending with <a href="/wiki/Gaoyang,_Hebei" title="Gaoyang, Hebei">Gaoyang</a> in Hubei Province) as 13 cities, 140 towns and 1350 villages either flooded or were partially flooded by the reservoir [A_2-M:CR3-1HP:S-15],<sup id="cite_ref-124" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-124">[124]</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-autogenerated3_125-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-autogenerated3-125">[125]</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-126" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-126">[126]</a></sup> about 1.5% of the province's 60.3&#160;million and <a href="/wiki/Chongqing" title="Chongqing">Chongqing</a> Municipality's 31.44&#160;million population.<sup id="cite_ref-MWC_News_101307_127-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-MWC_News_101307-127">[127]</a></sup> About 140,000&#160;residents were relocated to other provinces.<sup id="cite_ref-chinadaily2_128-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-chinadaily2-128">[128]</a></sup></p>
<p>Relocation was completed on July 22, 2008.<sup id="cite_ref-autogenerated3_125-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-autogenerated3-125">[125]</a></sup> Some 2007 reports claimed that Chongqing Municipality will encourage an additional four&#160;million people to move away from the dam to the main urban area of Chongqing by 2020.<sup id="cite_ref-bbc12102007_129-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-bbc12102007-129">[129]</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-xinhua11102007_130-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-xinhua11102007-130">[130]</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-xinhua26092007_131-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-xinhua26092007-131">[131]</a></sup> However, the municipal government explained that the relocation is due to urbanization, rather than the dam, and people involved included other areas of the municipality.<sup id="cite_ref-ccdv20071116_132-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-ccdv20071116-132">[132]</a></sup></p>
<p>Allegedly, funds for relocating 13,000 farmers around Gaoyang disappeared after being sent to the local government, leaving residents without compensation.<sup id="cite_ref-nationalgeographic_133-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-nationalgeographic-133">[133]</a></sup></p>
<h2><span class="mw-headline" id="Other_effects">Other effects</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Three_Gorges_Dam&amp;action=edit&amp;section=23" title="Edit section: Other effects">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h2>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Culture_and_aesthetics">Culture and aesthetics</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Three_Gorges_Dam&amp;action=edit&amp;section=24" title="Edit section: Culture and aesthetics">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
<p>The 600&#160;km (370&#160;mi) long reservoir flooded some 1,300&#160;archaeological sites and altered the appearance of the Three Gorges as the water level rose over 300&#160;ft (91&#160;m).<sup id="cite_ref-134" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-134">[134]</a></sup> Cultural and historical relics are being moved to higher ground as they are discovered, but the flooding inevitably covered undiscovered relics. Some sites could not be moved because of their location, size, or design. For example, the <a href="/wiki/Hanging_coffins" title="Hanging coffins">hanging coffins</a> site high in the <a href="/wiki/Shen_Nong_Stream" class="mw-redirect" title="Shen Nong Stream">Shen Nong Gorge</a> is part of the cliffs.<sup id="cite_ref-Hogan_135-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Hogan-135">[135]</a></sup></p>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="National_security">National security</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Three_Gorges_Dam&amp;action=edit&amp;section=25" title="Edit section: National security">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
<p>The <a href="/wiki/United_States_Department_of_Defense" title="United States Department of Defense">United States Department of Defense</a> reported that in <a href="/wiki/Taiwan" title="Taiwan">Taiwan</a>, "proponents of strikes against the mainland apparently hope that merely presenting credible threats to China's urban population or high-value targets, such as the Three Gorges Dam, will deter Chinese military coercion."<sup id="cite_ref-136" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-136">[136]</a></sup></p>
<p>The notion that the <a href="/wiki/Military_of_the_Republic_of_China" class="mw-redirect" title="Military of the Republic of China">military in Taiwan</a> would seek to destroy the dam provoked an angry response from the mainland Chinese media. <a href="/wiki/People%27s_Liberation_Army" title="People's Liberation Army">People's Liberation Army</a> General <a href="/wiki/Liu_Yuan_(politician)" class="mw-redirect" title="Liu Yuan (politician)">Liu Yuan</a> was quoted in the <i><a href="/wiki/China_Youth_Daily" title="China Youth Daily">China Youth Daily</a></i> saying that the People's Republic of China would be "seriously on guard against threats from <a href="/wiki/Taiwan_independence" class="mw-redirect" title="Taiwan independence">Taiwan independence</a> terrorists."<sup id="cite_ref-137" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-137">[137]</a></sup></p>
<p>The three gorge dam is a steel-concrete <a href="/wiki/Gravity_dam" title="Gravity dam">gravity dam</a>. The water is held back by the innate mass of the individual dam sections. As a result, damage to an individual section should not affect other parts of the dam. Due to the sheer size of the dam, it is expected to withstand tactical nuclear strikes.<sup id="cite_ref-138" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-138">[138]</a></sup></p>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Structural_integrity">Structural integrity</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Three_Gorges_Dam&amp;action=edit&amp;section=26" title="Edit section: Structural integrity">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
<p>Days after the first filling of the reservoir, around 80 hairline cracks were observed in the dam's structure.<sup id="cite_ref-139" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-139">[139]</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-140" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-140">[140]</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-141" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-141">[141]</a></sup> The submerged spillway gates of the dam might pose a risk of <a href="/wiki/Cavitation" title="Cavitation">cavitation</a>, similar to that which severely damaged the poorly designed and cavitating spillways of the <a href="/wiki/Glen_Canyon_Dam" title="Glen Canyon Dam">Glen Canyon Dam</a> in the US state of <a href="/wiki/Arizona" title="Arizona">Arizona</a>, which was unable to properly withstand the <a href="/wiki/Risks_of_the_Glen_Canyon_Dam#Colorado_River_Floods_of_1983" class="mw-redirect" title="Risks of the Glen Canyon Dam">Colorado river floods of 1983</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-142" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-142">[142]</a></sup> However 163,000 concrete units of the Three Gorges dam all passed quality testing and the deformation was within design limits. An experts group gave the project overall a good quality rating.<sup id="cite_ref-143" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-143">[143]</a></sup></p>
<h2><span class="mw-headline" id="Upstream_dams">Upstream dams</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Three_Gorges_Dam&amp;action=edit&amp;section=27" title="Edit section: Upstream dams">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h2>
<div class="thumb tright">
<div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a href="/wiki/File:Yangtze_longitudinal_profile_upstream.JPG" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/6/6d/Yangtze_longitudinal_profile_upstream.JPG/220px-Yangtze_longitudinal_profile_upstream.JPG" width="220" height="125" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/6/6d/Yangtze_longitudinal_profile_upstream.JPG/330px-Yangtze_longitudinal_profile_upstream.JPG 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/6/6d/Yangtze_longitudinal_profile_upstream.JPG/440px-Yangtze_longitudinal_profile_upstream.JPG 2x" data-file-width="1122" data-file-height="638" /></a>
<div class="thumbcaption">
<div class="magnify"><a href="/wiki/File:Yangtze_longitudinal_profile_upstream.JPG" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a></div>
Longitudinal profile of upstream Yangtze River</div>
</div>
</div>
<p>In order to maximize the utility of the Three Gorges Dam and cut down on sedimentation from the <a href="/wiki/Jinsha_River" title="Jinsha River">Jinsha River</a>, the upper course of the Yangtze River, authorities plan to build a series of dams on the Jinsha, including <a href="/wiki/Wudongde_Dam" title="Wudongde Dam">Wudongde Dam</a>, <a href="/wiki/Baihetan_Dam" title="Baihetan Dam">Baihetan Dam</a>, along with the now completed <a href="/wiki/Xiluodu_Dam" title="Xiluodu Dam">Xiluodu</a> and <a href="/wiki/Xiangjiaba_Dam" title="Xiangjiaba Dam">Xiangjiaba</a> dams. The total capacity of those four dams is 38,500&#160;MW,<sup id="cite_ref-144" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-144">[144]</a></sup> almost double the capacity of the Three Gorges.<sup id="cite_ref-145" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-145">[145]</a></sup> Baihetan is preparing for construction and Wudongde is seeking government approval. Another eight dams are in the midstream of the Jinsha and eight more upstream of it.<sup id="cite_ref-146" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-146">[146]</a></sup></p>
<div style="clear:both;"></div>
